Liebling soon joined and the group took on the Pentagram moniker as they began performing <br />\r\nLiebling&#39;s material from the previous Pentagram line-up. Griffin <br />\r\nthen met Hasselvander and relocated Death Row to the northern Virginia area and began playing together. After the <br />\r\ntrio began rehearsals without a singer, Hasselvander introduced Griffin to Liebling. After only one jam session <br />\r\ntogether, Liebling joined as vocalist for Death Row. Former Pentagram member Martin Swaney soon replaced Lee <br />\r\nAbney on bass and the classic Death Row line up was forged. Following demos recorded in 1982 and 1983, <br />\r\nHasselvander left the band, Stuart Rose was chosen as his replacement, and the band changed their name to <br />\r\nPentagram. The band was working towards <br />\r\nrecording a third album, but shortly after their first live performance, they imploded yet again. \r\n</p>\r\n<p>\r\nIn 1993, the &quot;Death Row&quot; line-up of Bobby, Victor, Joe, and Marty reformed when Peaceville Records reissued the <br />\r\nfirst two albums. With additional Peaceville support, they went on to release their third full-length album, &quot;Be <br />\r\nForewarned&quot; in 1994.
